<DIV align="left"><A NAME="000"></A></DIV>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Item&nbsp;7.01 Regulation FD Disclosure</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On November 29, 2004, Atrium
Companies, Inc. (&#147;ACI&#148;)
announced that it and its parent, Atrium Corporation (&#147;Atrium
Corp.&#148;), intend to effect a comprehensive refinancing plan that
will lower overall interest expense as well as extend debt
maturities. The elements of the proposed plan are: (i) ACI entering
into a new senior secured credit facility; and (ii) the issuance of
senior discount notes (the &#147;notes&#148;) by a newly formed
wholly-owned subsidiary of the ACI (&#147;ACIH&#148;), which
subsidiary will subsequently become a direct subsidiary of Atrium
Corp., the parent entity of ACI, through a distribution of the
capital stock of ACIH and the contribution of the net proceeds from
such issuance to ACI. ACIH intends to raise approximately $124.9 million of
gross proceeds through the private placement of the notes,
subject to market and other conditions. The net proceeds from the
proposed plan are expected to be used to consummate a cash tender
offer and consent solicitation for all of ACI's outstanding
10<sup style="font-size: 80%; vertical-align: top;">1</sup>/<small>2</small>%
Senior Subordinated Notes due 2009 (the &#147;Existing Notes&#148;) and to repay all outstanding
borrowings under ACI's existing senior secured credit facility. ACI
commenced the tender offer and consent solicitation on December 7,
2004.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;References
to &#147;the Company&#148;, &#147;we&#148;, &#147;our&#148;,
&#147;ours&#148; and &#147;us&#148; refer collectively to ACIH
together with its consolidated subsidiaries and predecessors as a
combined entity.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This
Current Report on Form 8-K (&#147;Current Report&#148;) contains
certain forward-looking statements (as such term is defined in the
Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995) relating to us
based on beliefs of management that involve substantial risks and
uncertainties. When used in this Current Report, the words
&#147;anticipate&#148;, &#147;believe&#148;, &#147;estimate&#148;,
&#147;expect&#148;, &#147;intend&#148; and other similar expressions,
as they relate to us or our management, identify forward-looking
statements. Such statements reflect our current views with respect to
the risks and uncertainties regarding our operations and results of
operations, as well as our customers and suppliers, including the
availability of credit; competition within our industry; interest
rate fluctuations; employment trends; changes in levels of consumer
confidence and preferences; national and regional trends in new
housing starts; costs of compliance with environmental, health and
safety laws; protection of our intellectual property; costs for
labor, land and raw materials; pricing pressures; impact of
construction defect and home warranty claims; shifts in market demand
and general economic conditions. Should one or more of these risks or
uncertainties materialize, or should underlying assumptions or
estimates prove incorrect, actual sales may vary materially from
those described herein as anticipated, believed, estimated, expected
or intended. In addition to specific factors described in connection
with any particular forward-looking statement, factors that could
cause actual results to differ materially include, but are not
limited to, those in the &#147;Risk factors&#148; section. Other
risks besides those listed in &#147;Risk factors&#148; also could
adversely affect us. We disclaim any obligation to publicly update or
revise any forward-looking statements.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
notes will not be registered under the Securities Act of 1933 (the &#147;Securities Act&#148;),
or any state securities laws, and unless so registered, may not be offered or sold in the United
States except pursuant to an exemption from, or in a transaction not subject to, the registration
requirements of the Securities Act and applicable state securities laws. This press release does
not constitute an offer to sell or the solicitation of an offer to buy any security and shall not
constitute an offer, solicitation or sale in any jurisdiction in which such offering would be
unlawful.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In connection with the
 issuance of the notes by ACIH, the following information will be disclosed to
potential investors.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>

<B><FONT size="2"> 1</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>
<P align="left">
<FONT size="4">THE REFINANCING</FONT>

<DIV align="left">
<FONT size="2">We intend to effect a refinancing plan (the
&#147;Refinancing&#148;) that will decrease our ongoing debt
service requirements, extend the average life of our
indebtedness and provide for greater financial and operational
flexibility. The elements of the Refinancing (including the
payment of related costs and expenses) are:
</FONT>
</DIV>
<P>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="1%"></TD>
    <TD width="99%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <I><FONT size="2">Restructuring.</FONT></I><FONT size="2"> Prior
    to the issuance of the notes, ACI will form&nbsp;ACIH,
    which initially will be a wholly-owned subsidiary of ACI, and
    ACIH will then form a new wholly-owned subsidiary of ACIH
    (&#147;New Subsidiary&#148;). Immediately after ACI enters into
    the new credit facility and repays all borrowings under
    ACI&#146;s existing credit facility and ACIH issues the notes, ACI will dividend the capital stock of ACIH to
    Atrium Corp. and, following such dividend, ACI will merge with
    New Subsidiary, with ACI being the surviving entity of such
    merger. The formation of ACIH and New Subsidiary, the dividend
    by ACI of the capital stock of ACIH to Atrium Corp. and the
    merger of ACI with New Subsidiary are collectively referred to
    herein as the &#147;Restructuring.&#148;
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <I><FONT size="2">New Credit Facility.</FONT></I><FONT size="2">
    In connection with the Refinancing, ACI intends to enter into
    a new credit facility which is expected to provide for
    (i)&nbsp;a new revolving facility of up to $50.0&nbsp;million,
    and (ii)&nbsp;a new $325.0&nbsp;million term loan facility.
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <I><FONT size="2">Repayment of Borrowings Under Existing Credit
    Facility.</FONT></I><FONT size="2"> In connection with the
Refinancing, ACI intends to repay in full all borrowings
    (consisting of existing revolving loans and existing term loans
    estimated to be approximately $198.6&nbsp;million as of
    September&nbsp;30, 2004) under its existing credit facility.
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <I><FONT size="2">The Notes.</FONT></I><FONT size="2"> In
connection with the Refinancing, ACIH
intends to issue the notes
    (gross proceeds of $124,916,721) and
    contribute the proceeds therefrom (net of the initial
    purchasers&#146; discounts and commissions and transaction
    expenses) to ACI as the surviving entity in the merger with New
    Subsidiary.
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <I><FONT size="2">Tender Offer and Consent
    Solicitation.</FONT></I><FONT size="2"> ACI intends to
    consummate a tender offer and consent solicitation for all of
    its Existing Notes and intends to redeem any Existing Notes that
    are not tendered pursuant to the tender offer. We commenced the
    tender offer and consent solicitation on December&nbsp;7, 2004.
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">2</FONT></B>
</DIV>




<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>


<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">The effectiveness of ACI&#146;s new credit
facility is a condition to the issuance of the notes.
ACI&#146;s entrance into the new credit facility is subject to
negotiation, execution and delivery of final documentation and
final approval by the lenders party thereto.
</FONT>


<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">In connection with the Refinancing, we intend to
amend our existing accounts receivable securitization facility
to increase the amounts committed under the facility to
$60.0&nbsp;million, add certain subsidiaries as originators and
amend the covenants so that they are substantially similar to
the covenants that will be contained in our new credit facility.
The effectiveness of the amendment to the covenants is a
condition to the issuance of the notes.
</FONT>



<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<B><FONT size="2"> 3</FONT></B>
</DIV>

    <TD><FONT size="2">(1)</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <I><FONT size="2">Pro forma consolidated financial data for the
    twelve months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004 were derived by
    (a)&nbsp;accumulating ACI&#146;s historical data for this period
    by summing reported results for the nine months ended
    September&nbsp;30, 2004 with ACI&#146;s reported results for the
    three months ended December&nbsp;31, 2003, (b)&nbsp;accumulating
    the historical results of the 2004 Acquisitions (defined below) and the 2003
    Acquisitions (defined below) from October&nbsp;1, 2003
    through their respective acquisition dates, (c)&nbsp;applying
    pro forma adjustments related to the 2004 Acquisitions and the
    2003 Acquisitions to present them as if they had occurred on
    October&nbsp;1, 2003, and (d)&nbsp;applying pro forma
    adjustments to present the December&nbsp;10, 2003 merger of KAT
Holdings, Inc. with Atrium Corp. with Atrium Corp. as the surviving
corporation (the &#147;2003 Merger&#148;) and the Refinancing as if
    it had occurred on October&nbsp;1, 2003, including the
    application of &#147;pushdown accounting.&#148;</FONT></I></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">(2)</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <I><FONT size="2">Amortization expense decreased $11,000 from
    $14,410 during 2001 to $3,410 during 2002. The decrease was
    primarily attributable to our adoption of Statement of
    Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;142, &#147;Goodwill and Other
    Intangible Assets,&#148; which eliminates the amortization of
    goodwill and subjects it to annual impairment tests.</FONT></I></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">(3)</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <I><FONT size="2">We estimate that capital expenditures will
    approximate $20,000 to $22,000 for the year ended
    December&nbsp;31, 2004.</FONT></I></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">(4)</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <I><FONT size="2">EBITDA represents net income (loss) before
    interest expense, securitization expense, income taxes,
    depreciation and amortization. Adjusted EBITDA represents EBITDA
    (as defined above) before stock compensation expense and special
    charges. While we do not intend for EBITDA or Adjusted EBITDA to
    represent cash flow from operations as defined by generally
    accepted accounting principles (&#147;GAAP&#148;) and we do not
    suggest that you consider them as indicators of operating
    performance or alternatives to cash flow or operating income (as
    measured by GAAP) or as measures of liquidity, we include them
    herein to provide additional information with respect to our
    ability to meet our future debt service, capital expenditures
    and working capital requirements. We believe EBITDA and Adjusted
    EBITDA provide investors and analysts in the building materials
    industry the necessary information to analyze and compare our
    historical results on a comparable basis with other companies on
    the basis of operating performance, leverage and liquidity.
    However, as EBITDA and Adjusted EBITDA are not defined by GAAP,
    they may not be calculated on the same basis as other similarly
    titled measures of other companies within the building materials
    industry.</FONT></I></TD>
</TR>
<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>
</Table>

<P align="left">
<A name='102'></A>

<!-- link1 "Risk factors" -->
<DIV align="left"><A NAME="001"></A></DIV>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="4">RISK FACTORS
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Substantial Leverage and Debt Service&#151;Our
substantial indebtedness could adversely affect our financial
health and prevent us from fulfilling our obligations under the
notes.</FONT></B>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">We are a highly leveraged company. After giving
effect to the Refinancing, at September&nbsp;30, 2004, we would
have had consolidated total debt plus amounts outstanding under
our off-balance sheet accounts receivable securitization
facility outstanding of approximately $500.0&nbsp;million, of
which approximately $375.1&nbsp;million would have been
indebtedness of ACIH&#146;s subsidiaries. After giving effect to
the Refinancing, at September&nbsp;30, 2004, our consolidated
total debt plus amounts outstanding under our accounts
receivable securitization facility as a percentage of
capitalization, would have been approximately 66.3%. After
giving effect to the transactions described under
&#147;Unaudited pro forma consolidated financial data,&#148; our
cash interest and securitization expense obligations in respect
of our total consolidated debt plus amounts outstanding under
our accounts receivable securitization facility for the latest
twelve months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004 would have been
approximately $33.1&nbsp;million. Our new credit facility and
the indenture governing the notes will permit us and certain of
our subsidiaries to incur certain additional indebtedness. After
giving effect to the Refinancing, at September&nbsp;30, 2004,
ACI could have borrowed an additional $39.4&nbsp;million under
its new credit facility and accounts receivable securitization
facility. We expect to increase the committed amounts under our
accounts receivable securitization facility by
$10.0&nbsp;million in connection with the Refinancing.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">Our high level of indebtedness could have
important consequences such&nbsp;as:
</FONT>
<P>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="1%"></TD>
    <TD width="99%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <FONT size="2">limiting our ability to obtain additional
    financing to fund our growth strategy, working capital, capital
    expenditures, debt service requirements or other purposes;
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <FONT size="2">limiting our ability to use operating cash flow
    in other areas of our business because we must dedicate a
    substantial portion of these funds to make principal payments
    and fund debt service requirements;
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <FONT size="2">increasing our vulnerability to interest
    fluctuations because, pro forma for the Refinancing,
    approximately $365.8&nbsp;million of our debt would have been at
    variable interest rates as of September&nbsp;30, 2004;
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <FONT size="2">limiting our ability to compete with others who
    are not as highly leveraged as we are;&nbsp;and
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <FONT size="2">limiting out ability to react to changing market
    conditions, changes in our industry and economic downturns.
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>



<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>
<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>

<DIV align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">8</FONT></B>
</DIV>

    <TD><FONT size="2">(6)</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <I><FONT size="2">Assumes that all of the Existing Notes are tendered and accepted for payment on or prior to December&nbsp;21, 2004.
For any Existing Notes not tendered and accepted for payment, instead of paying a tender premium and a consent fee, the Company, because it is redeeming all such
Existing Notes, will pay a redemption premium plus accrued and unpaid interest
for the 30-day notice period ending on the redemption date. This will result in a net additional payment by the Company at the end of such 30-day
notice period of $7.50 per $1,000 of principal amount of Existing Notes not tendered and accepted for payment.</FONT></I></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>


<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">(7)</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <I><FONT size="2">Represents transaction expenses which will be
    capitalized as deferred financing costs upon completion of the
    Refinancing.</FONT></I></TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>

Existing Notes, will pay a redemption premium plus accrued and unpaid interest
for the 30-day notice period ending on the redemption date. This will result in a net additional payment by the Company at the end of such 30-day

<DIV align="left"><A NAME="004"></A></DIV>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="4">UNAUDITED PRO FORMA CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL DATA
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">The following unaudited pro forma consolidated
balance sheet and consolidated statements of operations of ACIH
are based on ACI&#146;s historical consolidated financial
statements and the historical consolidated financial statements
of ACI&#146;s acquired entities adjusted to give effect to:
</FONT>
<P>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="1%"></TD>
    <TD width="99%"></TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <FONT size="2">the Refinancing, as if it had occurred on
    January&nbsp;1, 2003 with respect to the statements of
    operations and September&nbsp;30, 2004 with respect to the
    balance sheet;
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <FONT size="2">the 2003 Merger, as if it had occurred on
    January&nbsp;1, 2003;
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>

<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top">
    <TD><FONT size="2">&#149;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
    <TD align="left">
    <FONT size="2">the application of &#147;pushdown
    accounting&#148; pursuant to Staff Accounting Bulletin
    (&#147;SAB&#148;) No.&nbsp;54, &#147;Application of
    &#147;Pushdown&#148; Accounting Relating to the Acquisition of
    Certain Subsidiaries&#148; (&#147;SAB&nbsp;54&#148;), as if it
    had occurred on January&nbsp;1, 2003 with respect to the
    statements of operations and September&nbsp;30, 2004 with
    respect to the balance sheet. In connection with the 2003
    Merger, we did not apply &#147;pushdown accounting.&#148; The
    guidance in SAB&nbsp;No.&nbsp;54 allows post-merger financial
    statements to continue under the historical basis of accounting
    if significant public debt (e.g., the Existing Notes) remains
    outstanding. Pursuant to the Refinancing, the Existing Notes
    will be retired in their entirety. Upon such retirement of the
    Existing Notes, we will be required to apply &#147;pushdown
    accounting&#148;;
    </FONT></TD>
</TR>


<TR>
    <TD>&nbsp;</TD>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>


<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Notes to Unaudited Pro Forma Consolidated
Balance Sheet (all dollars in thousands)</FONT></B>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">(a)&nbsp;Represents the net cash outlay that
would have been required if the Refinancing had occurred on
September&nbsp;30, 2004.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">(b)&nbsp;In connection with the 2003 Merger, we
did not apply &#147;pushdown accounting&#148; pursuant to
SAB&nbsp;No.&nbsp;54. Pursuant to the Refinancing, the Existing
Notes will be retired and &#147;pushdown accounting&#148; will
be required. Therefore, the 2003 Merger has been accounted for
under the purchase method of accounting in accordance with
Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;142,
&#147;Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets&#148; (&#147;SFAS
No.&nbsp;142&#148;).
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">The estimated fair value adjustments associated
with pushdown accounting are as follows:
</FONT>

<CENTER>
<TABLE width="70%" align="center" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" border="0">

<TR>
    <TD width="85%"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>

<FONT size="2">The tender premium and consent payments on the Existing Notes assumes that all outstanding Existing
Notes are tendered and accepted for payment on or prior to December&nbsp;21, 2004. For any Existing Notes not tendered and accepted for payment, instead of
paying a tender premium and a consent fee, the Company, because it is redeeming all such Existing Notes, will pay a redemption premium plus accrued and unpaid interest for the 30-day notice period ending
on the redemption date. This will result in a net additional payment by the Company at the end of such
30-day notice period of $7.50 per $1,000 of principal amount of Existing Notes not tendered and accepted for payment.

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Notes to Unaudited Pro Forma Consolidated
Statements of Operations</FONT></B>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">(a)&nbsp;EBITDA represents net income (loss)
before interest expense, securitization expense, income taxes,
depreciation and amortization. Adjusted EBITDA represents EBITDA
(as defined below) before stock compensation expense and special
charges. While we do not intend for EBITDA or Adjusted EBITDA to
represent cash flow from operations as defined by GAAP and we do
not suggest that you consider them as indicators of operating
performance or alternatives to cash flow or operating income (as
measured by GAAP) or as measures of liquidity, we include them
to provide additional information with respect to our ability to
meet our future debt service, capital expenditures and working
capital requirements. We believe EBITDA and Adjusted EBITDA
provide investors and analysts in the building materials
industry the necessary information to analyze and compare our
historical results on a comparable basis with other companies on
the basis of operating performance, leverage and liquidity.
However, as EBITDA and Adjusted EBITDA are not defined by GAAP,
they may not be calculated on the same basis as other similarly
titled measures of other companies within the building materials
industry. For a reconciliation of net income to EBITDA as
reported for the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004 and
the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2003, see ACI&#146;s Quarterly
Report on Form&nbsp;10-Q for the quarterly period ended
September&nbsp;30, 2004 and ACI&#146;s Annual Report on
Form&nbsp;10-K for the fiscal year ended December&nbsp;31, 2003,
as amended by the amendment thereto filed with the Commission on
April&nbsp;9, 2004, respectively.
</FONT>

<FONT size="2">(1)&nbsp;The pro forma special charges of $12,996
incurred during the twelve months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004
included $4,000 of charges for the vesting of warrants issued to
Mr.&nbsp;Hull, $553 of charges for management retention bonuses
to be paid on or after December&nbsp;10, 2004, $6,407 of
management transaction bonuses, $1,226 related to the
termination of a consulting agreement with the former owner of
Ellison Windows and $810 for stock option compensation related
to options outstanding prior to the 2003 Merger. The pro forma
special charges of $10,059 incurred during 2003 represented
expenses associated with the 2003 Merger, which included $6,407
of management transaction bonuses, $1,615 of warrants issued to
Mr.&nbsp;Hull, $1,226 related to the termination of a consulting
agreement with the former owner of Ellison Windows and $811 for
stock option compensation related to options outstanding prior
to the 2003 Merger. The pro forma special charges of $2,938
incurred during the nine&nbsp;months ended September&nbsp;30,
2004 included $2,385 of charges for the vesting of warrants
issued to Mr.&nbsp;Hull and $553 of charges for accrued
management retention bonuses to be paid on or after
December&nbsp;10, 2004.
</FONT>

<FONT size="2">(2)&nbsp;Pro forma Adjusted EBITDA for the twelve
months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004 does not include addbacks
for non-cash LIFO expense of $2,183, a one-time inventory
write-down at Kinco of $634, management fees paid to the former
shareholders of Kinco of $231 and compensation paid to the
former owner of Superior of $156, totaling $3,204.

<DIV align="left"><A NAME="005"></A></DIV>
<P align="left">
<FONT size="4">MANAGEMENT
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">The following information was disclosed regarding Mark
Blanchat, Ronald J. Foy and Christopher Birosak.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<I><FONT size="2">Mark Blanchat </FONT></I><FONT size="2">has
served as Executive Vice President of Strategy and Development
of Atrium Corp. and ACI since June 2004. Mr. Blanchat became the
Executive Vice President of Strategy and Development of ACIH in
December 2004. Prior to June 2004, Mr.&nbsp;Blanchat served as
Vice President of Corporate Development and Vice President of
Operations of Jeld-Wen Windows and Doors since 1997. Prior to
joining Jeld-Wen, Mr.&nbsp;Blanchat served in various capacities
with First Southwest Securities and GE Capital.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<I><FONT size="2">Ronald J. Foy </FONT></I><FONT size="2">has
served as Group President of Eastern Operations of Atrium Corp.
and ACI since September 2004. Prior to September 2004,
Mr.&nbsp;Foy was with Masco Corp. since 1995, and most recently
served as Divisional President of the Bath and Shower Group and
Divisional President of the Hardware Group. Prior to 1995,
Mr.&nbsp;Foy was with Black and Decker in various positions from
1981 to 1994.
</FONT>

<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>
<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>


<DIV align="center">
<B><FONT size="2"> 28</FONT></B>
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>


<P align="left">
<I><FONT size="2">Christopher Birosak
</FONT></I><FONT size="2">has served as a Director of Atrium
Corp. and ACI since September 2004, and became a Director of
ACIH in December 2004. Mr.&nbsp;Birosak is a Managing Director
of Merrill Lynch&nbsp;&#38; Co., Inc. and since July 2004 has
worked in the Global Private Equity Division of Merrill Lynch.
From 1994 to June 2004, Mr.&nbsp;Birosak served as Managing
Director in the Leveraged Finance Group of Merrill Lynch.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="4">PRINCIPAL STOCKHOLDERS
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">Upon the issuance of the notes, all of
ACI&#146;s issued and outstanding common stock will be owned by
ACIH. The following table sets forth certain information
regarding the beneficial ownership of Atrium Corp.&#146;s common
stock as of November&nbsp;30, 2004, by each person who
beneficially owns more than 5% of the outstanding common stock
of Atrium Corp. and by the directors and certain executive
officers of Atrium Corp. Unless otherwise indicated below, to
our knowledge, all persons listed below have sole voting and
investment power with respect to their shares of Atrium
Corp.&#146;s common stock.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">The amounts and percentages of common stock
beneficially owned are reported on the basis of regulations of
the Commission governing the determination of beneficial
ownership of securities. Under the rules of the Commission, a
person is deemed to be a &#147;beneficial owner&#148; of a
security if that person has or shares &#147;voting power,&#148;
which includes the power to vote or to direct the voting of such
security, or &#147;investment power,&#148; which includes the
power to dispose of or direct the disposition of such security.
A person is also deemed to be a beneficial owner of any
securities of which that person has a right to acquire
beneficial ownership within 60&nbsp;days. All persons listed
have sole voting and investment power with respect to their
shares unless otherwise indicated.
</FONT>
